      <p>On 10 September 2012, parliament elected <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Sheikh_Mohamud" title="Hassan Sheikh Mohamud">Hassan Sheikh Mohamud</a> as the new President of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> President Mohamud later appointed <a href="/wiki/Abdi_Farah_Shirdon" title="Abdi Farah Shirdon">Abdi Farah Shirdon</a> as the new Prime Minister on 6 October 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> who was succeeded in office by <a href="/wiki/Abdiweli_Sheikh_Ahmed" title="Abdiweli Sheikh Ahmed">Abdiweli Sheikh Ahmed</a> on 21 December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> On 17 December 2014, former Premier <a href="/wiki/Omar_Abdirashid_Ali_Sharmarke" class="mw-redirect" title="Omar Abdirashid Ali Sharmarke">Omar Abdirashid Ali Sharmarke</a> was reappointed Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Somalia" title="Judiciary of Somalia">Judiciary of Somalia</a> is defined by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Somalia" title="Constitution of Somalia">Provisional Constitution</a> of the Federal Republic of Somalia. Adopted on 1 August 2012 by a National Constitutional Assembly in Mogadishu,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> the document was formulated by a committee of specialists chaired by attorney and incumbent Speaker of the Federal Parliament, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Osman_Jawari" title="Mohamed Osman Jawari">Mohamed Osman Jawari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> It provides the legal foundation for the existence of the Federal Republic and source of legal authority.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national court structure is organized into three tiers: the Constitutional Court, Federal Government level courts and <a href="/wiki/States_and_regions_of_Somalia" title="States and regions of Somalia">State</a> level courts. A nine-member Judicial Service Commission appoints any Federal tier member of the judiciary. It also selects and presents potential Constitutional Court judges to the House of the People of the Federal Parliament for approval. If endorsed, the President appoints the candidate as a judge of the Constitutional Court. The five-member Constitutional Court adjudicates issues pertaining to the constitution, in addition to various Federal and sub-national matters.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somali law draws from a mixture of three different systems: <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xeer" title="Xeer">customary law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the collapse of Somalia in 1991, there were no relations or any contact between the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Somaliland" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Somaliland">Somaliland government</a>, which declared itself a country and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Somalia">government of Somalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Somalia" title="Foreign relations of Somalia">Foreign relations of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_(16176887607).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg/220px-2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg/330px-2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg/440px-2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_%2816176887607%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3682" data-file-height="2450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2015_01_25_Turkish_President_Visit_to_Somalia-1_(16176887607).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former President of Somalia <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Sheikh_Mohamud" title="Hassan Sheikh Mohamud">Hassan Sheikh Mohamud</a> with Turkish President <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdogan</a> opening the new terminal of Aden Abdulle International Airport in Mogadishu, Somalia.(25 January 2015)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somalia's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Somalia" title="Foreign relations of Somalia">foreign relations</a> are handled by the President as the head of state, the Prime Minister as the head of government, and the federal <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Somalia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Somalia)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mogturkemb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mogturkemb.jpg/220px-Mogturkemb.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mogturkemb.jpg/330px-Mogturkemb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mogturkemb.jpg/440px-Mogturkemb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="817"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mogturkemb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkish</a> embassy in Mogadishu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to Article 54 of the national constitution, the allocation of powers and resources between the Federal Government and the Federal Republic of Somalia's constituent Federal Member States shall be negotiated and agreed upon by the Federal Government and the Federal Member States, except in matters pertaining to foreign affairs, national defence, citizenship and immigration, and monetary policy. Article 53 also stipulates that the Federal Government shall consult the Federal Member States on major issues related to international agreements, including negotiations vis-a-vis foreign trade, finance and treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> The Federal Government maintains <a href="/wiki/Bilateralism" title="Bilateralism">bilateral relations</a> with a number of other central governments in the international community. Among these are <a href="/wiki/Djibouti%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Djibouti–Somalia relations">Djibouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Ethiopia–Somalia relations">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Egypt–Somalia relations">Egypt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93United_Arab_Emirates_relations" title="Somalia–United Arab Emirates relations">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93Yemen_relations" title="Somalia–Yemen relations">Yemen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Somalia–Turkey relations">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Italy–Somalia relations">Italy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Somalia–United Kingdom relations">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Denmark–Somalia relations">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/France%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="France–Somalia relations">France</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Somalia–United States relations">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="China–Somalia relations">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" title="Japan–Somalia relations">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Somalia_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Russia–Somalia relations">Russian Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia%E2%80%93South_Korea_relations" title="Somalia–South Korea relations">South Korea</a>. </p>
      <p>Additionally, Somalia has several <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Somalia" title="List of diplomatic missions of Somalia">diplomatic missions</a> abroad. There are likewise various <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Somalia" title="List of diplomatic missions in Somalia">foreign embassies and consulates</a> based in the capital Mogadishu and elsewhere in the country. </p>
      <p>Somalia is also a member of many international organizations, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, African Union and <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>. It was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> Other memberships include the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Authority_on_Development" title="Intergovernmental Authority on Development">Intergovernmental Authority on Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="International Bank for Reconstruction and Development">International Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">International Civil Aviation Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Association" title="International Development Association">International Development Association</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Corporation" title="International Finance Corporation">International Finance Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Federation_of_Trade_Unions" title="World Federation of Trade Unions">World Federation of Trade Unions</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somali_Armed_Forces" title="Somali Armed Forces">Somali Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_(16739095620).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg/220px-2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg/330px-2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg/440px-2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_%2816739095620%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1064"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2015_03_25_SNA_PASSOUT-5_(16739095620).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Instructors from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Training_Mission_in_Somalia" title="European Union Training Mission in Somalia">European Union Training Mission in Somalia</a> (EUTM) take Somali soldiers through training drills at Jazeera Training Camp in Mogadishu.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Somali_Armed_Forces" title="Somali Armed Forces">Somali Armed Forces</a> (SAF) are the military forces of the Federal Republic of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> Headed by the President as Commander in Chief, they are constitutionally mandated to ensure the nation's sovereignty, independence and territorial integrity.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The SAF was initially made up of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_National_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali National Army">Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Navy" title="Somali Navy">Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Air_Force" title="Somali Air Force">Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Police_Force" title="Somali Police Force">Police Force</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Service_(Somalia)" title="National Security Service (Somalia)">National Security Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> In the post-independence period, it grew to become among the largest militaries on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-Ramsbotham_222_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramsbotham_222-114">[113]</a></sup> The subsequent outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">civil war</a> in 1991 led to the disbandment of the Somali National Army.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, the gradual process of reconstituting the military was put in motion with the establishment of the Transitional Federal Government (TFG). The Somali Armed Forces are now overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Somalia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Somalia)">Ministry of Defence</a> of the Federal Government of Somalia, formed in mid-2012. In January 2013, the Somali federal government also re-opened the national intelligence service in Mogadishu, renaming the agency the <a href="/wiki/National_Intelligence_and_Security_Agency" title="National Intelligence and Security Agency">National Intelligence and Security Agency</a> (NISA).<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_Armed_Forces" title="Somaliland Armed Forces">Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puntland_Security_Force" title="Puntland Security Force">Puntland</a> regional governments maintain their own security and police forces. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Somalia" title="Human rights in Somalia">Human rights in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Both male and female <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Somalia" title="LGBT rights in Somalia">same-sex sexual activity</a> is illegal and could be <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_for_homosexuality" title="Capital punishment for homosexuality">punished by up to death</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On October 3, 2020, a <a href="/wiki/UN" class="mw-redirect" title="UN">UN</a> human rights investigator raised concerns over Somali government's backtracking of human rights commitments. According to information collected by the investigator, Somali authorities were regressing on commitments to protect peoples’ economic, social and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_rights" title="Cultural rights">cultural rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Somalia" title="Economy of Somalia">Economy of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg/220px-Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg/330px-Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg/440px-Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg 2x" data-file-width="826" data-file-height="521"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Air_Somalia_Tupolev_Tu-154.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Air_Somalia" title="Air Somalia">Air Somalia</a> Tupolev <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154" title="Tupolev Tu-154">Tu-154</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah (city)">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>. Somalia today has several private airlines
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Somalia" title="Central Bank of Somalia">Central Bank of Somalia</a>, despite experiencing civil unrest, Somalia has maintained a healthy informal <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a>, based mainly on <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittance</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wire_transfer" title="Wire transfer">money transfer</a> companies and <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Somalia" title="Communications in Somalia">telecommunications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> Due to a dearth of formal government statistics and the recent <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">civil war</a>, it is difficult to gauge the size or growth of the economy. For 1994, the CIA estimated the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> at $3.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> In 2001, it was estimated to be $4.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> By 2009, the CIA estimated that the GDP had grown to $5.731 billion, with a projected real growth rate of 2.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> According to a 2007 <a href="/wiki/British_Chambers_of_Commerce" title="British Chambers of Commerce">British Chambers of Commerce</a> report, the private sector also grew, particularly in the service sector. Unlike the pre-civil war period when most services and the industrial sector were <a href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Government-owned corporation">government-run</a>, there has been substantial, albeit unmeasured, private investment in commercial activities; this has been largely financed by the <a href="/wiki/Somali_diaspora" title="Somali diaspora">Somali diaspora</a>, and includes trade and marketing, money transfer services, transportation, communications, fishery equipment, airlines, telecommunications, education, health, construction and hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-Brcc_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brcc-229">[228]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">Libertarian</a> economist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Leeson" title="Peter Leeson">Peter Leeson</a> attributes this increased economic activity to the Somali <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" title="Customary law">customary law</a> (referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Xeer" title="Xeer">Xeer</a></i>), which he suggests provides a stable environment to conduct business in.<sup id="cite_ref-Petletbet_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petletbet-230">[229]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_(27469932863).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg/220px-2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg/330px-2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg/440px-2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_%2827469932863%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2016_04_Eid_Preparions-11_(27469932863).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Shoppers in Hamarwayne market in Mogadishu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the Central Bank of Somalia, the country's GDP per capita as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is $226, a slight reduction in real terms from 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> About 43% of the population lives on less than 1 US dollar a day, with around 24% of those found in urban areas and 54% living in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somalia's economy consists of both traditional and modern production, with a gradual shift toward modern industrial techniques. Somalia has the largest population of camels in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEA._RosatiA._TewoldeC._Mosconi2007_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEA._RosatiA._TewoldeC._Mosconi2007-232">[231]</a></sup> According to the Central Bank of Somalia, about 80% of the population are nomadic or semi-nomadic pastoralists, who keep goats, sheep, camels and cattle. The nomads also gather resins and gums to supplement their income.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Somalia" title="Agriculture in Somalia">Agriculture in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Agriculture is the most important economic sector of Somalia. It accounts for about 65% of the GDP and employs 65% of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-Brcc_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brcc-229">[228]</a></sup> Livestock contributes about 40% to GDP and more than 50% of export earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> Other principal exports include <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charcoal" title="Charcoal">charcoal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> are products for the domestic market.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> According to the Central Bank of Somalia, imports of goods total about $460 million per year, surpassing aggregate imports prior to the start of the civil war in 1991. Exports, which total about $270 million annually, have also surpassed pre-war aggregate export levels. Somalia has a trade deficit of about $190 million per year, but this is exceeded by remittances sent by Somalis in the diaspora, estimated to be about $1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the advantage of being located near the Arabian Peninsula, Somali traders have increasingly begun to challenge <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>'s traditional dominance over the Gulf Arab livestock and meat market, offering quality animals at very low prices. In response, Gulf Arab states have started to make strategic investments in the country, with <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> building livestock export infrastructure and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> purchasing large farmlands.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> Somalia is also a major world supplier of <a href="/wiki/Frankincense" title="Frankincense">frankincense</a> and <a href="/wiki/Myrrh" title="Myrrh">myrrh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bosaso_port.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bosaso_port.jpg/220px-Bosaso_port.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bosaso_port.jpg/330px-Bosaso_port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bosaso_port.jpg/440px-Bosaso_port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="422"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bosaso_port.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bosaso" title="Port of Bosaso">Port of Bosaso</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The modest <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">industrial sector</a>, based on the processing of agricultural products, accounts for 10% of Somalia's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Somali Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Somali Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a>, over six private <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> firms also offer commercial flights to both domestic and international locations, including <a href="/wiki/Daallo_Airlines" title="Daallo Airlines">Daallo Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jubba_Airways" title="Jubba Airways">Jubba Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Express_Airways" title="African Express Airways">African Express Airways</a>, East Africa 540, Central Air and Hajara.<sup id="cite_ref-Scca_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scca-235">[234]</a></sup> In 2008, the Puntland government signed a multimillion-dollar deal with <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>'s Lootah Group, a regional industrial group operating in the Middle East and Africa. According to the agreement, the first phase of the investment is worth <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_dirham" title="United Arab Emirates dirham">Dhs</a> 170&nbsp;m and will see a set of new companies established to operate, manage and build <a href="/wiki/Bosaso" title="Bosaso">Bosaso</a>'s free trade zone and sea and airport facilities. The Bosaso Airport Company is slated to develop the airport complex to meet international standards, including a new 3,400&nbsp;m (11,200&nbsp;ft) runway, main and auxiliary buildings, taxi and apron areas, and security perimeters.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to the outbreak of the civil war in 1991, the roughly 53 state-owned small, medium and large manufacturing firms were foundering, with the ensuing conflict destroying many of the remaining industries. However, primarily as a result of substantial local investment by the Somali diaspora, many of these small-scale plants have re-opened and newer ones have been created. The latter include fish-canning and meat-processing plants in the northern regions, as well as about 25 factories in the Mogadishu area, which manufacture <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mineral_water" title="Mineral water">mineral water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confectionery" title="Confectionery">confections</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bag" title="Plastic bag">plastic bags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">fabric</a>, hides and skins, <a href="/wiki/Detergent" title="Detergent">detergent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">soap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>, foam <a href="/wiki/Mattress" title="Mattress">mattresses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pillow" title="Pillow">pillows</a>, fishing <a href="/wiki/Boat" title="Boat">boats</a>, carry out packaging, and <a href="/wiki/Stonemasonry" title="Stonemasonry">stone processing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Somtroap_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somtroap-237">[236]</a></sup> In 2004, an $8.3 million <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> bottling plant also opened in the city, with investors hailing from various constituencies in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">Foreign investment</a> also included multinationals including <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company">Dole Fruit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monetary_and_payment_system">Monetary and payment system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Monetary and payment system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Somalia" title="Central Bank of Somalia">Central Bank of Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somali_shilling" title="Somali shilling">Somali shilling</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Central Bank of Somalia is the official <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">monetary authority</a> of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> In terms of financial management, it is in the process of assuming the task of both formulating and implementing <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Monpol_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monpol-240">[239]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Owing to a lack of confidence in the local currency, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US dollar</a> is widely accepted as a medium of exchange alongside the Somali shilling. <a href="/wiki/Dollarization" class="mw-redirect" title="Dollarization">Dollarization</a> notwithstanding, the large issuance of the Somali shilling has increasingly fuelled price hikes, especially for low value transactions. According to the Central Bank, this inflationary environment is expected to come to an end as soon as the bank assumes full control of monetary policy and replaces the presently circulating currency introduced by the private sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Monpol_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monpol-240">[239]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although Somalia has had no central monetary authority for more than 15 years between the outbreak of the civil war in 1991 and the subsequent re-establishment of the Central Bank of Somalia in 2009, the nation's payment system is fairly advanced primarily due to the widespread existence of private <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Somalia#Finance" title="Economy of Somalia">money transfer operators</a> (MTO) that have acted as informal banking networks.<sup id="cite_ref-Paysys_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paysys-241">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These remittance firms (<i><a href="/wiki/Hawala" title="Hawala">hawalas</a></i>) have become a large industry in Somalia, with an estimated US$1.6 billion annually remitted to the region by <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somalis</a> in the diaspora via money transfer companies.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> Most are members of the Somali Money Transfer Association (SOMTA), an umbrella organization that regulates the community's money transfer sector, or its predecessor, the Somali Financial Services Association (SFSA).<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Towhamrec_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Towhamrec-243">[242]</a></sup> The largest of the Somali MTOs is <a href="/wiki/Dahabshiil" title="Dahabshiil">Dahabshiil</a>, a Somali-owned firm employing more than 2,000 people across 144 countries with branches in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Towhamrec_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Towhamrec-243">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somshil5r.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Somshil5r.jpg/220px-Somshil5r.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Somshil5r.jpg/330px-Somshil5r.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Somshil5r.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="202"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somshil5r.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>500 <a href="/wiki/Somali_shilling" title="Somali shilling">Somali shilling</a> banknote
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As the reconstituted Central Bank of Somalia fully assumes its monetary policy responsibilities, some of the existing money transfer companies are expected in the near future to seek licenses so as to develop into full-fledged commercial banks. This will serve to expand the national payments system to include formal cheques, which in turn is expected to reinforce the efficacy of the use of monetary policy in domestic <a href="/wiki/Macroeconomics" title="Macroeconomics">macroeconomic</a> management.<sup id="cite_ref-Paysys_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paysys-241">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With a significant improvement in local security, Somali expatriates began returning to the country for investment opportunities. Coupled with modest foreign investment, the inflow of funds have helped the Somali shilling increase considerably in value. By March 2014, the currency had appreciated by almost 60% against the U.S. dollar over the previous 12 months. The Somali shilling was the strongest among the 175 global currencies traded by <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a>, rising close to 50 percentage points higher than the next most robust global currency over the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Somalia_Stock_Exchange" title="Somalia Stock Exchange">Somalia Stock Exchange</a> (SSE) is the national <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">bourse</a> of Somalia. It was founded in 2012 by the Somali diplomat <a href="/wiki/Idd_Mohamed" title="Idd Mohamed">Idd Mohamed</a>, Ambassador extraordinary and deputy permanent representative to the United Nations. The SSE was established to attract investment from both Somali-owned firms and global companies in order to accelerate the ongoing post-conflict reconstruction process in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[244]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_and_natural_resources">Energy and natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Energy and natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mineral_industry_of_Somalia" title="Mineral industry of Somalia">Mineral industry of Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oil_exploration_in_Puntland" title="Oil exploration in Puntland">Oil exploration in Puntland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The World Bank reports that <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> is now in large part supplied by local businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-Brcc_229-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brcc-229">[228]</a></sup> Among these domestic firms is the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Energy_Company" title="Somali Energy Company">Somali Energy Company</a>, which performs generation, transmission and distribution of electric power.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[245]</a></sup> In 2010, the nation produced 310 million kWh and consumed 288.3 million kWh of electricity, ranked 170th and 177th, respectively, according to the CIA.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Puntland_oil.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Puntland_oil.png/290px-Puntland_oil.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Puntland_oil.png/435px-Puntland_oil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Puntland_oil.png 2x" data-file-width="570" data-file-height="599"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Puntland_oil.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Oil_exploration_in_Puntland" title="Oil exploration in Puntland">Oil blocks</a> in Puntland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somalia has reserves of several natural resources, including <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. The CIA reports that there are 5.663 billion cubic metres of proven natural gas reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The presence or extent of proven oil reserves in Somalia is uncertain. The CIA asserts that as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are no proven reserves of oil in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/UNCTAD" class="mw-redirect" title="UNCTAD">UNCTAD</a> suggests that most proven oil reserves in Somalia lie off its northwestern coast, in the Somaliland region.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[246]</a></sup> An oil group listed in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Range_Resources" title="Range Resources">Range Resources</a>, estimates that the Puntland region in the northeast has the potential to produce 5 billion barrels (790<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) to 10 billion barrels (1.6<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>9</sup>&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil,<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[247]</a></sup> compared to the 6.7 billion barrels of proven oil reserves in Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[248]</a></sup> As a result of these developments, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_Petroleum_Corporation" title="Somalia Petroleum Corporation">Somalia Petroleum Corporation</a> was established by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[249]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 1960s, UN geologists also discovered major uranium deposits and other rare mineral reserves in Somalia. The find was the largest of its kind, with industry experts estimating that the amount of the deposits could amount to over 25% of the world's then known uranium reserves of 800,000 tons.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[250]</a></sup> In 1984, the IUREP Orientation Phase Mission to Somalia reported that the country had 5,000 tons of uranium reasonably assured resources (RAR), 11,000 tons of uranium estimated additional resources (EAR) in <a href="/wiki/Calcrete" class="mw-redirect" title="Calcrete">calcrete</a> deposits, as well as 0–150,000 tons of uranium speculative resources (SR) in <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> and calcrete deposits.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[251]</a></sup> Somalia evolved into a major world supplier of uranium, with American, UAE, Italian and Brazilian mineral companies vying for extraction rights. Link Natural Resources has a stake in the central region, and Kilimanjaro Capital has a stake in the 1,161,400 acres (470,002&nbsp;ha) Amsas-Coriole-Afgoi (ACA) Block, which includes uranium exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Trans-National_Industrial_Electricity_and_Gas_Company" title="Trans-National Industrial Electricity and Gas Company">Trans-National Industrial Electricity and Gas Company</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> based in Mogadishu. It unites five major Somali companies from the <a href="/wiki/Commerce" title="Commerce">trade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Security" title="Security">security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> sectors, following a 2010 joint agreement signed in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> to provide electricity and gas infrastructure in Somalia. With an initial investment budget of $1 billion, the company launched the Somalia Peace Dividend Project, a labour-intensive energy program aimed at facilitating local industrialization initiatives. </p>
      <p>According to the Central Bank of Somalia, as the nation embarks on the path of reconstruction, the economy is expected to not only match its pre-civil war levels, but also to accelerate in growth and development due to Somalia's untapped natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbsef_41-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbsef-41">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somalia is endowed with renewable energy resources and ranked no. 13 out of 156 countries in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index) which implies that countries at the top of the ranking are likely to benefit geopolitically after the global transition to renewable energy is completed.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[253]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications_and_Media">Telecommunications and Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Telecommunications and Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Somalia" title="Communications in Somalia">Communications in Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Somalia">Media of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hormuud.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hormuud.jpg/170px-Hormuud.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hormuud.jpg/255px-Hormuud.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/Hormuud.jpg 2x" data-file-width="281" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hormuud.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Hormuud_Telecom" title="Hormuud Telecom">Hormuud Telecom</a> building in Mogadishu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the start of the civil war, various new telecommunications companies began to spring up and compete to provide missing infrastructure. Funded by Somali entrepreneurs and backed by expertise from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> and Europe, these nascent telecommunications firms offer affordable <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> and Internet services that are not available in many other parts of the continent. Customers can conduct <a href="/wiki/Electronic_funds_transfer" title="Electronic funds transfer">money transfers</a> (such as through the popular <a href="/wiki/Dahabshiil" title="Dahabshiil">Dahabshiil</a>) and other <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banking</a> activities via mobile phones, as well as easily gain wireless Internet access.<sup id="cite_ref-Telfirm_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telfirm-255">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After forming partnerships with multinational corporations such as <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Nextel" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprint Nextel">Sprint</a>, <a href="/wiki/ITT_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="ITT Corporation">ITT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telenor" title="Telenor">Telenor</a>, these firms now offer the cheapest and clearest phone calls in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup> These Somali telecommunication companies also provide services to every city and town in Somalia. There are presently around 25 mainlines per 1,000 persons, and the local availability of telephone lines (<i>tele-density</i>) is higher than in neighbouring countries; three times greater than in adjacent Ethiopia.<sup id="cite_ref-Somtroap_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somtroap-237">[236]</a></sup> Prominent Somali telecommunications companies include <a href="/wiki/Golis_Telecom_Somalia" title="Golis Telecom Somalia">Golis Telecom Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hormuud_Telecom" title="Hormuud Telecom">Hormuud Telecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somafone" title="Somafone">Somafone</a>, <a href="/wiki/NationLink_Telecom" title="NationLink Telecom">Nationlink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netco_(Somalia)" title="Netco (Somalia)">Netco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telcom_(Somalia)" title="Telcom (Somalia)">Telcom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somali_Telecom_Group" title="Somali Telecom Group">Somali Telecom Group</a>. Hormuud Telecom alone grosses about $40 million a year. Despite their rivalry, several of these companies signed an inter-connectivity deal in 2005 that allows them to set prices, maintain and expand their networks, and ensure that competition does not get out of control.<sup id="cite_ref-Telfirm_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telfirm-255">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Investment in the telecom industry is held to be one of the clearest signs that Somalia's economy has continued to develop despite civil strife in parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Telfirm_255-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telfirm-255">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The state-run <a href="/wiki/Somali_National_Television" title="Somali National Television">Somali National Television</a> is the principal national public service TV channel. After a twenty-year hiatus, the station was officially re-launched on 4 April 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup> Its radio counterpart <a href="/wiki/Radio_Mogadishu" title="Radio Mogadishu">Radio Mogadishu</a> also broadcasts from the capital. <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_National_TV" title="Somaliland National TV">Somaliland National TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puntland_TV_and_Radio" title="Puntland TV and Radio">Puntland TV and Radio</a> air from the northern regions. </p>
      <p>Additionally, Somalia has several private television and radio networks. Among these are <a href="/wiki/Horn_Cable_Television" title="Horn Cable Television">Horn Cable Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Television_(Somalia)" title="Universal Television (Somalia)">Universal TV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> The political Xog Doon and Xog Ogaal and Horyaal Sports broadsheets publish out of the capital. There are also a number of online media outlets covering local news,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Garowe_Online" title="Garowe Online">Garowe Online</a>, Wardheernews, and <a href="/wiki/Puntland_Post" title="Puntland Post">Puntland Post</a>. </p>
      <p>The internet <a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">country code top-level domain</a> (ccTLD) for Somalia is <a href="/wiki/.so" title=".so">.so</a>. It was officially relaunched on 1 November 2010 by .SO Registry, which is regulated by the nation's Ministry of Posts and Telecommunications.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[258]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 22 March 2012, the Somali Cabinet also unanimously approved the National Communications Act. The bill paves the way for the establishment of a National Communications regulator in the broadcasting and telecommunications sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2013, following a Memorandum of Understanding signed with <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Post" title="Emirates Post">Emirates Post</a> in April of the year, the federal Ministry of Posts and Telecommunications officially reconstituted the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Postal_Service" title="Somali Postal Service">Somali Postal Service</a> (Somali Post).<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[260]</a></sup> In October 2014, the ministry also relaunched postal delivery from abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup> The postal system is slated to be implemented in each of the country's 18 administrative provinces via a new postal coding and numbering system.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[262]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Somalia" title="Tourism in Somalia">Tourism in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Laas_Geel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Laas_Geel.jpg/220px-Laas_Geel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Laas_Geel.jpg/330px-Laas_Geel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Laas_Geel.jpg/440px-Laas_Geel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Laas_Geel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ancient cave paintings near Hargeisa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somalia has a number of local attractions, consisting of historical sites, beaches, waterfalls, mountain ranges and national parks. The tourist industry is regulated by the national Ministry of Tourism. The autonomous Puntland and Somaliland regions maintain their own tourism offices.<sup id="cite_ref-Ntmucig_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ntmucig-264">[263]</a></sup> The Somali Tourism Association (SOMTA) also provides consulting services from within the country on the national tourist industry.<sup id="cite_ref-SOMTA_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOMTA-265">[264]</a></sup> As of March 2015, the Ministry of Tourism and Wildlife of the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Southwestern Somalia">South West State</a> announced that it is slated to establish additional game reserves and wildlife ranges.<sup id="cite_ref-Gswstrghtat_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gswstrghtat-266">[265]</a></sup> The United States Government recommends travelers to not travel to Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[266]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Notable sights include the <a href="/wiki/Laas_Geel" title="Laas Geel">Laas Geel</a> caves containing Neolithic <a href="/wiki/Rock_art" title="Rock art">rock art</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Madow" title="Cal Madow">Cal Madow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golis_Mountains" title="Golis Mountains">Golis Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ogo_Mountains" title="Ogo Mountains">Ogo Mountains</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Iskushuban" title="Iskushuban">Iskushuban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lamadaya" title="Lamadaya">Lamadaya</a> waterfalls; and the <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa_National_Park" title="Hargeisa National Park">Hargeisa National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jilib_National_Park" title="Jilib National Park">Jilib National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kismayo_National_Park" title="Kismayo National Park">Kismayo National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lag_Badana_National_Park" title="Lag Badana National Park">Lag Badana National Park</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Somalia" title="Transport in Somalia">Transport in Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Somalia" title="List of airports in Somalia">List of airports in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg/220px-Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg/330px-Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg/440px-Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="682"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aden_Abdullah_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Aden_Adde_International_Airport" title="Aden Adde International Airport">Aden Adde International Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somalia's network of roads is 22,100&nbsp;km (13,700&nbsp;mi) long. As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 2,608&nbsp;km (1,621&nbsp;mi) streets are <a href="/wiki/Road_surface" title="Road surface">paved</a> and 19,492&nbsp;km (12,112&nbsp;mi) are unpaved.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> A 750&nbsp;km (470&nbsp;mi) highway connects major cities in the northern part of the country, such as <a href="/wiki/Bosaso" title="Bosaso">Bosaso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galkayo" title="Galkayo">Galkayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garowe" class="mw-redirect" title="Garowe">Garowe</a>, with towns in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[267]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Somali Civil Aviation Authority">Somali Civil Aviation Authority</a> (SOMCAA) is Somalia's national <a href="/wiki/Civil_aviation_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil aviation authority">civil aviation authority</a> body. After a long period of management by the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Caretaker_Authority_for_Somalia" title="Civil Aviation Caretaker Authority for Somalia">Civil Aviation Caretaker Authority for Somalia</a> (CACAS), SOMCAA is slated to re-assume control of Somalia's airspace by 31 December 2013. </p>
      <p>Sixty-two airports across Somalia accommodate aerial transportation; seven of these have paved runways. Among the latter, four airports have runways of over 3,047&nbsp;m; two are between 2,438&nbsp;m and 3,047&nbsp;m; and one is 1,524&nbsp;m to 2,437&nbsp;m long.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> There are fifty-five airports with unpaved landing areas. One has a runway of over 3,047&nbsp;m; four are between 2,438&nbsp;m and 3,047&nbsp;m in length; twenty are 1,524&nbsp;m to 2,437&nbsp;m; twenty-four are 914&nbsp;m to 1,523&nbsp;m; and six are under 914&nbsp;m.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> Major airports in the nation include the <a href="/wiki/Aden_Adde_International_Airport" title="Aden Adde International Airport">Aden Adde International Airport</a> in Mogadishu, the <a href="/wiki/Hargeisa_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hargeisa International Airport">Hargeisa International Airport</a> in Hargeisa, the <a href="/wiki/Kismayo_Airport" title="Kismayo Airport">Kismayo Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baidoa_Airport" title="Baidoa Airport">Baidoa Airport</a> in Baidoa, and the <a href="/wiki/Bender_Qassim_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bender Qassim International Airport">Bender Qassim International Airport</a> in Bosaso. </p>
      <p>Established in 1964, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Airlines" title="Somali Airlines">Somali Airlines</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> of Somalia. It suspended operations during the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[269]</a></sup> However, a reconstituted Somali government later began preparations in 2012 for an expected relaunch of the airline,<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[270]</a></sup> with the first new Somali Airlines aircraft scheduled for delivery by the end of December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Somali Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Somali Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a>, the void created by the closure of Somali Airlines has since been filled by various Somali-owned private carriers. Over six of these private airline firms offer commercial flights to both domestic and international locations, including <a href="/wiki/Daallo_Airlines" title="Daallo Airlines">Daallo Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jubba_Airways" title="Jubba Airways">Jubba Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Express_Airways" title="African Express Airways">African Express Airways</a>, East Africa 540, Central Air and Hajara.<sup id="cite_ref-Scca_235-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scca-235">[234]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Possessing the longest coastline on the continent,<sup id="cite_ref-FactbookCoastline_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FactbookCoastline-13">[12]</a></sup> Somalia has several major <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaports</a>. Maritime transport facilities are found in the port cities of Mogadishu, Bosaso, <a href="/wiki/Berbera" title="Berbera">Berbera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merca" title="Merca">Merca</a>. There is also one <a href="/wiki/Merchant_marine" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant marine">merchant marine</a>. Established in 2008, it is cargo-based.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Somalia" title="Demographics of Somalia">Demographics of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-16">[15]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">2.3 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">9.0 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">15 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Somalia had an estimated population of around 15 million inhabitants in 2018;<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-16">[15]</a></sup> the total population according to the 1975 census was 3.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> survey conducted in 2013 and 2014 estimated the total population to be 12,316,895.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 85% of local residents are <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">ethnic Somalis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> who have historically inhabited the northern part of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullahi_2001_8_11_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullahi_2001_8_11-19">[18]</a></sup> They have traditionally been organized into nomadic pastoral clans, loose empires, sultanates and city-states.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullahi_2001_138_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullahi_2001_138-275">[274]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">Civil strife</a> in the early 1990s greatly increased the size of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_diaspora" title="Somali diaspora">Somali diaspora</a>, as many of the best educated Somalis left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Non-Somali ethnic minority groups make up the remainder of Somalia's population, and are largely concentrated in the southern regions.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullahi_2001_8_11_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullahi_2001_8_11-19">[18]</a></sup> They include <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_people" title="Bravanese people">Bravanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Bantu" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali Bantu">Bantus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_of_Ethiopia" title="People of Ethiopia">Ethiopians</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Oromo_people" title="Oromo people">Oromos</a>), <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Yemen" title="Demographics of Yemen">Yemenis</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somalis" title="Italian Somalis">Italians</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">Britons</a>. The Bantus, the largest ethnic minority group in Somalia, are the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Somalia" title="Slavery in Somalia">slaves</a> who were brought in from southeastern Africa by Arab and Somali traders.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup> In 1940, there were about 50,000 <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somalis" title="Italian Somalis">Italians</a> living in Italian Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup> Most Europeans left after independence, while a small number of Westerners are still present in Somalia mainly working for <a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organizations</a> operating in Somalia. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png/280px-Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png/420px-Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png/560px-Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Population_pyramid_of_Somalia_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population per age group
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A sizable Somali diaspora exists in various <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western countries</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (in particular in the state of <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>) and in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (particularly in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, as well on the Arabian peninsula, and several African nations, such as <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. The Somali diaspora is deeply involved in the politics and development of Somalia. The president of Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Farmaajo" class="mw-redirect" title="Farmaajo">Mohamed Abdullahi Mohamed</a>, was a former diaspora Somali and held <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_United_States" title="Citizenship of the United States">US citizenship</a> which he voluntarily renounced in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[279]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somalia's population is expanding at a growth rate of 1.75% per annum and a birth rate of 40.87 births per 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Somalia is 6.08 children born per woman (2014 estimates), the fourth highest in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> Most local residents are young, with a median age of 17.7 years; about 44% of the population is between the ages of 0–14 years, 52.4% is between the ages of 15–64 years, and only 2.3% is 65 years of age or older.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sex_ratio" title="Sex ratio">gender ratio</a> is roughly balanced, with proportionally about as many men as women.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is little reliable statistical information on <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> in Somalia. Rough estimates have been made indicating a rate of urbanization of 4.79% per annum (2005–2010 est.), with many towns quickly growing into cities.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> Many ethnic minorities have also moved from rural areas to urban centres since the onset of the civil war, particularly to <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 37.7% of the nation's population live in towns and cities, with the percentage rapidly increasing.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Somalia" title="Languages of Somalia">Languages of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> are the official languages of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> The Somali language is the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali people">Somali people</a>, the nation's most populous ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">[2]</a></sup> It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Asiatic languages">Afro-Asiatic</a> language family, and its nearest relatives are the <a href="/wiki/Oromo_language" title="Oromo language">Oromo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afar_language" title="Afar language">Afar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saho_language" title="Saho language">Saho</a> languages.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup> Somali is the best documented of the Cushitic languages,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup> with academic studies of it dating from before 1900. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ciismaniya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Ciismaniya.jpg/220px-Ciismaniya.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/Ciismaniya.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="281" data-file-height="286"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ciismaniya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Osmanya_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Osmanya alphabet">Osmanya</a> writing script
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somali <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> are divided into three main groups: <a href="/wiki/Northern_Somali" title="Northern Somali">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benadiri_Somali" title="Benadiri Somali">Benadir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maay_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Maay language">Maay</a>. Northern Somali (or Northern-Central Somali) forms the basis for Standard Somali. Benadir (also known as Coastal Somali) is spoken on the <a href="/wiki/Benadir" class="mw-redirect" title="Benadir">Benadir</a> coast, from <a href="/wiki/Adale" title="Adale">Adale</a> to south of <a href="/wiki/Merca" title="Merca">Merca</a> including Mogadishu, as well as in the immediate hinterland. The coastal dialects have additional <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a> that do not exist in Standard Somali. Maay is principally spoken by the Digil and Mirifle (<a href="/wiki/Rahanweyn" title="Rahanweyn">Rahanweyn</a>) clans in the southern areas of Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup> Benadiri is the main dialect spoken in the country, in contrast to Northern Somali which is the main dialect spoken in Somaliland.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing systems</a> have been used over the years for transcribing the Somali language. Of these, the <a href="/wiki/Somali_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali alphabet">Somali alphabet</a> is the most widely used, and has been the official writing script in Somalia since the Supreme Revolutionary Council formally introduced it in October 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup> The script was developed by the Somali <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguist</a> <a href="/wiki/Shire_Jama_Ahmed" title="Shire Jama Ahmed">Shire Jama Ahmed</a> specifically for the Somali language, and uses all letters of the English Latin alphabet except <i>p</i>, <i>v</i> and <i>z</i>.
