Besides Ahmed's Latin script, other orthographies that have been used for centuries for writing Somali include the long-established <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">Arabic script</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wadaad_writing" title="Wadaad writing">Wadaad writing</a>. Indigenous writing systems developed in the 20th century include the <a href="/wiki/Osmanya_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Osmanya alphabet">Osmanya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borama_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Borama alphabet">Borama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kaddare_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaddare alphabet">Kaddare</a> scripts, which were invented by <a href="/wiki/Osman_Yusuf_Kenadid" title="Osman Yusuf Kenadid">Osman Yusuf Kenadid</a>, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Abdurahman_Sheikh_Nuur" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdurahman Sheikh Nuur">Abdurahman Sheikh Nuur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hussein_Sheikh_Ahmed_Kaddare" title="Hussein Sheikh Ahmed Kaddare">Hussein Sheikh Ahmed Kaddare</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to Somali, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> is an official national language in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> Around 2 million Somalis speak it<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[287]</a></sup> due to centuries-old ties with the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, the far-reaching influence of the Arabic media, and religious education.<sup id="cite_ref-Dubnov_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dubnov-289">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[290]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is widely spoken and taught. It used to be an administrative language in the British Somaliland protectorate and due to <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> is now also prominent across Somalia. English is the <a href="/wiki/Medium_of_instruction" title="Medium of instruction">medium of instruction</a> at many universities across Somalia,<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[292]</a></sup> and is one of the primary working languages of major <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a> operating in Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[295]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[296]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> was an official language in Italian Somaliland and during the trusteeship period, but its use significantly diminished following independence. It is now most frequently heard among older generations, government officials, and in educated circles.<sup id="cite_ref-Dubnov_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dubnov-289">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue.com_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue.com-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other minority languages include <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_dialect" title="Bravanese dialect">Bravanese</a>, a variant of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili language</a> that is spoken along the coast by the <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_people" title="Bravanese people">Bravanese people</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_dialect" title="Bajuni dialect">Kibajuni</a>, a Swahili dialect that is the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a> minority ethnic group. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg" class="image" title="Mogadishu"><img alt="Mogadishu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg/120px-Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="68" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg/180px-Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg/240px-Mogadishu_1_Somalia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:Hargskyl1.jpg" class="image" title="Hargeisa"><img alt="Hargeisa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hargskyl1.jpg/120px-Hargskyl1.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hargskyl1.jpg/180px-Hargskyl1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hargskyl1.jpg/240px-Hargskyl1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Hargeisa" title="Hargeisa">Hargeisa</a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">1</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Banaadir" title="Banaadir">Banaadir</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">2,120,000<sup id="cite_ref-Dwua_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dwua-298">[297]</a></sup></td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">11</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Afgooye" title="Afgooye">Afgooye</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Lower_Shebelle" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Shebelle">Lower Shebelle</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">79,400<sup id="cite_ref-tageo_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tageo-299">[298]</a></sup> </td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Somalia 2010<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a><sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:99.8%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">99.8%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:red; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.2%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Somalia" title="Religion in Somalia">Religion in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mosislsol2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mosislsol2.jpg/170px-Mosislsol2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mosislsol2.jpg/255px-Mosislsol2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mosislsol2.jpg/340px-Mosislsol2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="496"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mosislsol2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Islamic_Solidarity" title="Mosque of Islamic Solidarity">Mosque of Islamic Solidarity</a> in Mogadishu is the largest mosque in the Horn region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 99.8% of Somalia's population is <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup> The majority belong to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> school of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_jurisprudence" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic jurisprudence">Islamic jurisprudence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdullahi_2001_1_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdullahi_2001_1-21">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mysticism" title="Mysticism">mystical</a> sect of Islam, is also well established, with many local <i>jama'a</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Zaouia" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaouia">zawiya</a></i>) or congregations of the various <i><a href="/wiki/Tariqah" class="mw-redirect" title="Tariqah">tariiqa</a></i> or Sufi orders.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[305]</a></sup> The constitution of Somalia likewise defines Islam as the state religion of the Federal Republic of Somalia, and Islamic <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a> law as the basic source for national legislation. It also stipulates that no law that is inconsistent with the basic tenets of Shari'a can be enacted.<sup id="cite_ref-Frspc_216-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frspc-216">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Islam entered the region very early on, as a group of persecuted Muslims had sought refuge across the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> in the Horn of Africa at the urging of the Islamic prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[306]</a></sup> Islam may thus have been introduced into Somalia well before the faith even took root in its place of origin.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[307]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, the Somali community has produced numerous important Islamic sheikhs and clerics over the centuries, many of whom have significantly shaped the course of Muslim learning and practice in the Horn of Africa, the Arabian Peninsula, and well beyond. Among these Islamic scholars is the 14th-century Somali <a href="/wiki/Theologian" class="mw-redirect" title="Theologian">theologian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> <a href="/wiki/Uthman_bin_Ali_Zayla%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Uthman bin Ali Zayla'i">Uthman bin Ali Zayla'i</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zeila" title="Zeila">Zeila</a>, who wrote the single most authoritative text on the <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi</a> school of Islam, consisting of four volumes known as the <i>Tabayin al-Haqa'iq li Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq</i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is a minority religion in Somalia, with adherents representing less than 0.1% of the population in 2010 according to the Pew Research Center.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup> There is one <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> diocese for the whole country, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mogadiscio" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Mogadiscio">Diocese of Mogadishu</a>, which estimates that there were only about one hundred Catholic practitioners in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[308]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1913, during the early part of the colonial era, there were virtually no Christians in the Somali territories, with only about 100–200 followers coming from the schools and orphanages of the few Catholic missions in the <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a> <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[309]</a></sup> There were also no known Catholic missions in Italian Somaliland during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[310]</a></sup> In the 1970s, during the reign of Somalia's then <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> government, church-run schools were closed and <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> sent home. There has been no <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishop</a> in the country since 1989, and the <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu_Cathedral" title="Mogadishu Cathedral">cathedral</a> in Mogadishu was severely damaged during the civil war. In December 2013, the Ministry of Justice and Religious Affairs also released a directive prohibiting the celebration of Christian festivities in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[311]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the Pew Research Center, less than 0.1% of Somalia's population in 2010 were adherents of <a href="/wiki/Folk_religion" title="Folk religion">folk religions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup> These mainly consisted of some non-Somali ethnic minority groups in the southern parts of the country, who practice <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>. In the case of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Bantu" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali Bantu">Bantu</a>, these religious traditions were inherited from their ancestors in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Africa" title="Southeast Africa">Southeast Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[312]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Additionally, according to the Pew Research Center, less than 0.1% of Somalia's population in 2010 were adherents of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligion by country">unaffiliated with any religion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_305-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-305">[304]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Somalia" title="Healthcare in Somalia">Healthcare in Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Somalia" title="Child marriage in Somalia">Child marriage in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Until the collapse of the federal government in 1991, the organizational and administrative structure of Somalia's <a href="/wiki/Healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare">healthcare</a> sector was overseen by the Ministry of Health. Regional medical officials enjoyed some authority, but healthcare was largely centralized. The <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> government of former President of Somalia <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> had put an end to private medical practice in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[313]</a></sup> Much of the national budget was devoted to military expenditure, leaving few resources for healthcare, among other services.<sup id="cite_ref-Petletbet_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petletbet-230">[229]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somalia's public healthcare system was largely destroyed during the ensuing civil war. As with other previously nationalized sectors, informal providers have filled the vacuum and replaced the former government monopoly over healthcare, with access to facilities witnessing a significant increase.<sup id="cite_ref-ANEITMIS_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANEITMIS-315">[314]</a></sup> Many new healthcare centres, clinics, hospitals and pharmacies have in the process been established through home-grown Somali initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-ANEITMIS_315-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANEITMIS-315">[314]</a></sup> The cost of medical consultations and treatment in these facilities is low, at $5.72 per visit in health centres (with a population coverage of 95%), and $1.89–3.97 per outpatient visit and $7.83–13.95 per bed day in primary through tertiary hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[315]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Comparing the 2005–2010 period with the half-decade just prior to the outbreak of the conflict (1985–1990), <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> actually increased from an average of 47 years for men and women to 48.2 years for men and 51 years for women.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Udasom_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udasom-318">[317]</a></sup> Similarly, the number of one-year-olds fully immunized against <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a> rose from 30% in 1985–1990 to 40% in 2000–2005,<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wbunses_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wbunses-319">[318]</a></sup> and for <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, it grew nearly 20% from 31% to 50% over the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wbunses_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wbunses-319">[318]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The number of infants with low birth weight fell from 16 per 1,000 to 0.3, a 15% drop in total over the same time frame.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[319]</a></sup> Between 2005 and 2010 as compared to the 1985–1990 period, <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> per 1,000 births also fell from 152 to 109.6.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Udasom_318-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Udasom-318">[317]</a></sup> Significantly, maternal mortality per 100,000 births fell from 1,600 in the pre-war 1985–1990 half-decade to 1,100 in the 2000–2005 period.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[320]</a></sup> The number of physicians per 100,000 people also rose from 3.4 to 4 over the same time frame,<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wbunses_319-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wbunses-319">[318]</a></sup> as did the percentage of the population with access to sanitation services, which increased from 18% to 26%.<sup id="cite_ref-Uhdrsom01_317-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uhdrsom01-317">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wbunses_319-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wbunses-319">[318]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> data on the midwifery workforce, there is a total of 429 midwives (including nurse-midwives) in Somalia, with a density of one midwife per 1,000 live births. Eight midwifery institutions presently exist in the country, two of which are private. Midwifery education programs on average last from 12 to 18 months, and operate on a sequential basis. The number of student admissions per total available student places is a maximum 100%, with 180 students enrolled as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Midwifery is regulated by the government, and a license is required to practice professionally. A live registry is also in place to keep track of licensed midwives. In addition, midwives in the country are officially represented by a local midwives association, with 350 registered members.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[321]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg/220px-Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg/330px-Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg/440px-Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1982"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_boy_receives_a_polio_vaccination.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Somali boy receiving a <a href="/wiki/Polio_vaccine" title="Polio vaccine">polio</a> vaccination.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to a 2005 World Health Organization estimate, about 97.9% of Somalia's women and girls underwent <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">Female genital mutilation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[322]</a></sup> a pre-marital custom mainly endemic to the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">horn of Africa</a> and parts of the Near East.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[323]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[324]</a></sup> Encouraged by women in the community, it is primarily intended to protect chastity, deter promiscuity, and offer protection from assault.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[325]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[326]</a></sup> By 2013, UNICEF in conjunction with the Somali authorities reported that the prevalence rate among 1- to 14-year-old girls in the autonomous northern Puntland and Somaliland regions had dropped to 25% following a social and religious awareness campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[327]</a></sup> About 93% of Somalia's male population is also reportedly circumcised.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[328]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Somalia has one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> infection rates on the continent. This is attributed to the Muslim nature of Somali society and adherence of Somalis to Islamic morals.<sup id="cite_ref-RCTHIV_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCTHIV-330">[329]</a></sup> While the estimated HIV prevalence rate in Somalia in 1987 (the first case report year) was 1% of adults,<sup id="cite_ref-RCTHIV_330-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCTHIV-330">[329]</a></sup> a 2012 report from UNAIDS says that since 2004, estimates from 0.7% to 1% have been assumed.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[330]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although healthcare is now largely concentrated in the private sector, the country's public healthcare system is in the process of being rebuilt, and is overseen by the Ministry of Health. The Minister of Health is Qamar Adan Ali.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[331]</a></sup> The autonomous Puntland region maintains its own Ministry of Health,<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[332]</a></sup> as does the Somaliland region in northwestern Somalia.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[333]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some of the prominent healthcare facilities in the country are <a href="/wiki/East_Bardera_Mothers_and_Children%27s_Hospital" title="East Bardera Mothers and Children's Hospital">East Bardera Mothers and Children's Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abudwak_Maternity_and_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Abudwak Maternity and Children's Hospital">Abudwak Maternity and Children's Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edna_Adan_Maternity_Hospital" title="Edna Adan Maternity Hospital">Edna Adan Maternity Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Bardera_Maternity_Unit" title="West Bardera Maternity Unit">West Bardera Maternity Unit</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Somalia" title="Education in Somalia">Education in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the outbreak of the civil war in 1991, the task of running schools in Somalia was initially taken up by community education committees established in 94% of the local schools.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[334]</a></sup> Numerous problems had arisen with regard to access to education in rural areas and along gender lines, quality of educational provisions, responsiveness of school curricula, educational standards and controls, management and planning capacity, and financing. To address these concerns, educational policies are being developed that are aimed at guiding the scholastic process. In the autonomous Puntland region, the latter includes a gender sensitive national education policy compliant with world standards, such as those outlined in the Convention on the Rights of the Child (CRC) and the Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women (CEDAW).<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[335]</a></sup> Examples of this and other educational measures at work are the regional government's enactment of legislation aimed at securing the educational interests of girls,<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[336]</a></sup> promoting the growth of an <a href="/wiki/Early_childhood_education" title="Early childhood education">Early Childhood Development</a> (ECD) program designed to reach parents and care-givers in their homes as well as in the ECD centers for 0 to 5-year-old children,<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[337]</a></sup> and introducing incentive packages to encourage teachers to work in remote rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[338]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Somalia)" title="Ministry of Education (Somalia)">Ministry of Education</a> is officially responsible for education in Somalia, and oversees the nation's <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">technical and vocational</a> schools, as well as primary and technical <a href="/wiki/Teacher_education" title="Teacher education">teacher training</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nonformal_learning" title="Nonformal learning">non-formal education</a>. About 15% of the government's budget is allocated toward scholastic instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[339]</a></sup> The autonomous Puntland and Somaliland macro-regions maintain their own Ministries of Education. </p>
      <p>In 2006, Puntland was the second territory in Somalia after Somaliland to introduce free primary schools, with teachers now receiving their salaries from the Puntland administration.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[340]</a></sup> From 2005/2006 to 2006/2007, there was a significant increase in the number of schools in Puntland, up 137 institutions from just one year prior. During the same period, the number of classes in the region increased by 504, with 762 more teachers also offering their services.<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_education_survey_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_education_survey-342">[341]</a></sup> Total student enrollment increased by 27% over the previous year, with girls lagging only slightly behind boys in attendance in most regions. The highest class enrollment was observed in the northernmost <a href="/wiki/Bari,_Somalia" title="Bari, Somalia">Bari</a> region, and the lowest was observed in the under-populated Ayn region. The distribution of classrooms was almost evenly split between urban and rural areas, with marginally more pupils attending and instructors teaching classes in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_education_survey_342-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_education_survey-342">[341]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mogauniv1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Mogauniv1.jpg/220px-Mogauniv1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Mogauniv1.jpg/330px-Mogauniv1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Mogauniv1.jpg/440px-Mogauniv1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="659" data-file-height="441"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mogauniv1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mogadishu_University" title="Mogadishu University">Mogadishu University</a>'s main campus in Mogadishu.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Higher education in Somalia is now largely private. Several universities in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu_University" title="Mogadishu University">Mogadishu University</a>, have been scored among the 100 best universities in Africa in spite of the harsh environment, which has been hailed as a triumph for <a href="/wiki/Grass-roots" class="mw-redirect" title="Grass-roots">grass-roots</a> initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Somtroap_237-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Somtroap-237">[236]</a></sup> Other universities also offering higher education in the south include <a href="/wiki/Benadir_University" title="Benadir University">Benadir University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_National_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Somalia National University">Somalia National University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kismayo_University" title="Kismayo University">Kismayo University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gedo" title="University of Gedo">University of Gedo</a>. In Puntland, higher education is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Puntland_State_University" title="Puntland State University">Puntland State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Africa_University" title="East Africa University">East Africa University</a>. In Somaliland, it is provided by <a href="/wiki/Amoud_University" title="Amoud University">Amoud University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hargeisa" title="University of Hargeisa">University of Hargeisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somaliland_University_of_Technology" title="Somaliland University of Technology">Somaliland University of Technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burao_University" title="Burao University">Burao University</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Madrasah" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrasah">Qu'ranic schools</a> (also known as <i>dugsi quran</i> or <i>mal'aamad quran</i>) remain the basic system of traditional religious instruction in Somalia. They provide Islamic education for children, thereby filling a clear religious and social role in the country. Known as the most stable local, non-formal system of education providing basic religious and moral instruction, their strength rests on community support and their use of locally made and widely available teaching materials. The Qu'ranic system, which teaches the greatest number of students relative to other educational sub-sectors, is often the only system accessible to Somalis in nomadic as compared to urban areas. A study from 1993 found, among other things, that about 40% of pupils in Qur'anic schools were female. To address shortcomings in religious instruction, the Somali government on its own part also subsequently established the Ministry of Endowment and Islamic Affairs, under which Qur'anic education is now regulated.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[342]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Somalia" title="Culture of Somalia">Culture of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somali_cuisine" title="Somali cuisine">Somali cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_food.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Somali_food.jpg/220px-Somali_food.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Somali_food.jpg/330px-Somali_food.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Somali_food.jpg/440px-Somali_food.jpg 2x" data-file-width="581" data-file-height="386"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Somali_food.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Various types of popular <a href="/wiki/Somali_cuisine" title="Somali cuisine">Somali dishes</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The cuisine of Somalia, which varies from region to region, is a mixture of diverse culinary influences. It is the product of Somalia's rich tradition of trade and commerce. Despite the variety, there remains one thing that unites the various regional cuisines: all food is served <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">halal</a>. There are, therefore no <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> dishes, <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverages">alcohol</a> is not served, nothing that died on its own is eaten, and no blood is incorporated. <i>Qaddo</i> or lunch is often elaborate. </p>
      <p>Varieties of 'bariis' (<a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>), the most popular probably being <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">basmati</a>, usually act as the main dish. Spices including <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clove" title="Clove">cloves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salvia_officinalis" title="Salvia officinalis">garden sage</a> are used to add aromas to these different rice dishes. Somalis serve dinner as late as 9 pm. During <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_(calendar_month)" title="Ramadan (calendar month)">Ramadan</a>, the evening meal is often presented after <a href="/wiki/Tarawih" title="Tarawih">Tarawih</a> prayers; sometimes up to 11 pm. </p>
      <p>'Xalwo' (<a href="/wiki/Halva" title="Halva">halva</a>) is a popular <a href="/wiki/Confectionery" title="Confectionery">confection</a> reserved for special festive occasions, such as <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid</a> celebrations or wedding receptions. It is made from <a href="/wiki/Corn_starch" title="Corn starch">corn starch</a>, sugar, cardamom powder, <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> powder and <a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">ghee</a>. <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">Peanuts</a> are also sometimes added to enhance texture and flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[343]</a></sup> After meals, homes are traditionally perfumed using <a href="/wiki/Frankincense" title="Frankincense">frankincense</a> (<i>lubaan</i>) or <a href="/wiki/Incense" title="Incense">incense</a> (<i>cuunsi</i>), which is prepared inside an incense burner referred to as a <i><a href="/wiki/Dabqaad" title="Dabqaad">dabqaad</a></i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Somalia" title="Music of Somalia">Music of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Somalia has a rich musical heritage centred on traditional Somali <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>. Most Somali songs are <a href="/wiki/Pentatonic_scale" title="Pentatonic scale">pentatonic</a>. That is, they only use five <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(music)" title="Pitch (music)">pitches</a> per <a href="/wiki/Octave" title="Octave">octave</a> in contrast to a <a href="/wiki/Heptatonic_scale" title="Heptatonic scale">heptatonic</a> (seven note) scale like the <a href="/wiki/Major_scale" title="Major scale">major scale</a>. At first listen, Somali music might be mistaken for the sounds of nearby regions such as Ethiopia, Sudan or the Arabian Peninsula, but it is ultimately recognizable by its own unique tunes and styles. Somali songs are usually the product of collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Lyricist" title="Lyricist">lyricists</a> (<i>midho</i>), <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriters</a> (<i>laxan</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">singers</a> (<i>codka</i> or "voice").<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[344]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Somalia">Literature of Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Somali scholars have for centuries produced many notable examples of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_literature" title="Islamic literature">Islamic literature</a> ranging from poetry to <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">Hadith</a>. With the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Somali_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Somali alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> in 1972 as the nation's standard orthography, numerous contemporary Somali authors have also released novels, some of which have received worldwide acclaim. Of these modern writers, <a href="/wiki/Nuruddin_Farah" title="Nuruddin Farah">Nuruddin Farah</a> is the most celebrated. Books such as <i><a href="/wiki/From_a_Crooked_Rib" title="From a Crooked Rib">From a Crooked Rib</a></i> and <i>Links</i> are considered important literary achievements, works that have earned Farah, among other accolades, the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Neustadt_International_Prize_for_Literature" title="Neustadt International Prize for Literature">Neustadt International Prize for Literature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[345]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Farah_Mohamed_Jama_Awl" class="mw-redirect" title="Farah Mohamed Jama Awl">Faarax M.J. Cawl</a> is another prominent Somali writer who is best known for his <a href="/wiki/Dervish_movement_(Somali)" title="Dervish movement (Somali)">Dervish era</a> novel, <i>Ignorance is the enemy of love</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bile_Abdi_(482x321).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg/170px-Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg/255px-Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg/340px-Bile_Abdi_%28482x321%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="314"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bile_Abdi_(482x321).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abdi_Bile" title="Abdi Bile">Abdi Bile</a>, Somalia's most decorated athlete and holder of the most national records.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Somalia" title="Sports in Somalia">Sports in Somalia</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Somalia. Important domestic competitions are the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Somalia League">Somalia League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia_Cup" title="Somalia Cup">Somalia Cup</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_football_team" title="Somalia national football team">Somalia national football team</a> playing internationally. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> is also played in the country. The <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_1981" title="FIBA Africa Championship 1981">FIBA Africa Championship 1981</a> was hosted in Mogadishu from 15 to 23 December December 1981, during which the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Somalia national basketball team">national basketball team</a> received the bronze medal.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[346]</a></sup> The squad also takes part in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Pan_Arab_Games" title="Basketball at the Pan Arab Games">basketball event</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Arab_Games" title="Pan Arab Games">Pan Arab Games</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2013, a <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_bandy_team" title="Somalia national bandy team">Somalia national bandy team</a> was formed in <a href="/wiki/Borl%C3%A4nge" title="Borlänge">Borlänge</a>. It later participated in the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandy World Championship 2014">Bandy World Championship 2014</a> in <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shelekhov" title="Shelekhov">Shelekhov</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faisal_Jeylani_Aweys" title="Faisal Jeylani Aweys">Faisal Jeylani Aweys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Deq_Abdulle" title="Mohamed Deq Abdulle">Mohamed Deq Abdulle</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_taekwondo_team" title="Somalia national taekwondo team">national taekwondo team</a> took home a silver medal and fourth place, respectively, at the 2013 Open World <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a> Challenge Cup in <a href="/wiki/Tongeren" title="Tongeren">Tongeren</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Somali_Olympic_Committee" title="Somali Olympic Committee">Somali Olympic Committee</a> has devised a special support program to ensure continued success in future tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[347]</a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Jama" title="Mohamed Jama">Mohamed Jama</a> has won both world and European titles in <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Thai Boxing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[348]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somali_architecture" title="Somali architecture">Somali architecture</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gondereshe2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Gondereshe2008.jpg/220px-Gondereshe2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Gondereshe2008.jpg/330px-Gondereshe2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Gondereshe2008.jpg/440px-Gondereshe2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="331"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gondereshe2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">Citadel</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gondershe" title="Gondershe">Gondershe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Somali architecture is a rich and diverse tradition of engineering and design involving multiple types of constructions and edifices, such as <a href="/wiki/Stonemasonry" title="Stonemasonry">stone cities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">citadels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortresses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum" title="Mausoleum">mausoleums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">temples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tower" title="Tower">towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monuments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">megaliths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menhir" title="Menhir">menhirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolmen" title="Dolmen">dolmens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomb" title="Tomb">tombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">tumuli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">steles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cistern" title="Cistern">cisterns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(water_supply)" title="Aqueduct (water supply)">aqueducts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouses</a>. Spanning the country's ancient, medieval and early modern periods, it also embraces the fusion of Somalo-Islamic architecture with contemporary Western designs. </p>
      <p>In ancient Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Pyramid" title="Pyramid">pyramidical</a> structures known in Somali as <i>taalo</i> were a popular burial style, with hundreds of these <a href="/wiki/Dry_stone" title="Dry stone">dry stone</a> monuments scattered around the country today. Houses were built of <a href="/wiki/Ashlar" title="Ashlar">dressed stone</a> similar to the ones in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[349]</a></sup> There are also examples of courtyards and large stone walls enclosing settlements, such as the Wargaade Wall. </p>
      <p>The adoption of Islam in Somalia's early medieval history brought <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architectural influences</a> from <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>. This stimulated a shift in construction from dry stone and other related materials to <a href="/wiki/Coral_rag" title="Coral rag">coral</a> stone, <a href="/wiki/Mudbrick" title="Mudbrick">sun dried bricks</a>, and the widespread use of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> in Somali architecture. Many of the new architectural designs, such as mosques, were built on the ruins of older structures, a practice that would continue over and over again throughout the following centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[350]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Somalia" title="Outline of Somalia">Outline of Somalia</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Somalia-related_articles" title="Index of Somalia-related articles">Index of Somalia-related articles</a>
        <div style="clear:both;"></div></li>
      </ul>
